Aesthetic experience constitutes divine gift and cultural appreciation through faithful contemplation, requiring spiritual discernment and grateful reception according to Reformed aesthetic understanding.


*** Respuesta Ortodoxa


Aesthetic experience constitutes liturgical participation and mystical contemplation through iconic beauty, requiring spiritual purification and divine communion according to Orthodox aesthetic theology.


*** Respuesta Judia


Aesthetic experience constitutes divine creation appreciation and cultural expression through ethical sensitivity, requiring moral formation and communal participation according to Jewish aesthetic framework.


*** Respuesta Islamica


Aesthetic experience constitutes divine manifestation contemplation and spiritual elevation through geometric harmony, requiring moral purification and cultural refinement according to Islamic aesthetic tradition.


*** Respuesta Hindu


Aesthetic experience constitutes rasa realization and spiritual transformation through contemplative appreciation, requiring aesthetic cultivation and divine devotion according to Hindu aesthetic philosophy.


*** Respuesta Budista


Aesthetic experience constitutes mindful appreciation and liberation from attachment through compassionate awareness, requiring wisdom cultivation and aesthetic mindfulness according to Buddhist aesthetic understanding.


*** Respuesta Confuciana


Aesthetic experience constitutes moral cultivation and cultural refinement through virtue development, requiring educational formation and social harmony according to Confucian aesthetic tradition.


*** Respuesta Kantiana


Aesthetic experience constitutes disinterested judgment and reflective appreciation through imaginative play, requiring aesthetic community and universal validity according to Kantian aesthetic theory.


*** Respuesta Fenomenologica


Aesthetic experience constitutes lived encounter and embodied appreciation through intentional consciousness, requiring phenomenological description and experiential analysis according to phenomenological aesthetic framework.



** How do we judge artistic value?


*** Respuesta Catolica


Artistic value derives from transcendental beauty and moral formation through rational criteria, requiring prudential judgment and cultural discernment according to Thomistic aesthetic evaluation.


*** Respuesta Protestante


Artistic value derives from divine glorification and faithful expression through biblical criteria, requiring spiritual discernment and cultural responsibility according to Reformed aesthetic judgment.


*** Respuesta Ortodoxa


Artistic value derives from liturgical beauty and mystical contemplation through iconic criteria, requiring spiritual formation and traditional wisdom according to Orthodox aesthetic evaluation.


*** Respuesta Judia


Artistic value derives from ethical beauty and cultural expression through moral criteria, requiring communal discernment and cultural responsibility according to Jewish aesthetic judgment.


*** Respuesta Islamica


Artistic value derives from divine glorification and spiritual elevation through Islamic criteria, requiring moral guidance and cultural refinement according to Islamic aesthetic evaluation.


*** Respuesta Hindu


Artistic value derives from rasa experience and spiritual realization through aesthetic criteria, requiring contemplative appreciation and cultural wisdom according to Hindu aesthetic judgment.


*** Respuesta Budista


Artistic value derives from liberation from suffering and compassionate expression through wisdom criteria, requiring mindful appreciation and ethical discernment according to Buddhist aesthetic evaluation.


*** Respuesta Confuciana


Artistic value derives from moral cultivation and cultural refinement through virtue criteria, requiring educational formation and social harmony according to Confucian aesthetic judgment.


*** Respuesta Formalist


Artistic value derives from formal innovation and aesthetic properties through technical criteria, requiring artistic expertise and aesthetic education according to formalist evaluation framework.


*** Respuesta Institutional


Artistic value derives from cultural recognition and institutional validation through social criteria, requiring critical consensus and cultural authority according to institutional aesthetic theory.



** Is there a universal aesthetic sense?


*** Respuesta Catolica


Universal aesthetic sense exists through natural law and transcendental beauty, requiring rational development and cultural formation according to Thomistic aesthetic anthropology.


*** Respuesta Protestante


Universal aesthetic sense exists through divine image and creation appreciation, requiring spiritual formation and faithful cultivation according to Reformed aesthetic understanding.


*** Respuesta Ortodoxa


Universal aesthetic sense exists through divine image and liturgical participation, requiring spiritual purification and mystical contemplation according to Orthodox aesthetic anthropology.


*** Respuesta Judia


Universal aesthetic sense exists through divine image and ethical sensitivity, requiring moral formation and cultural development according to Jewish aesthetic understanding.


*** Respuesta Islamica


Universal aesthetic sense exists through fitrah and divine manifestation, requiring spiritual purification and cultural refinement according to Islamic aesthetic anthropology.


*** Respuesta Hindu


Universal aesthetic sense exists through consciousness and rasa capacity, requiring spiritual cultivation and aesthetic development according to Hindu aesthetic psychology.


*** Respuesta Budista


Universal aesthetic sense exists through Buddha-nature and compassionate awareness, requiring mindfulness cultivation and wisdom development according to Buddhist aesthetic understanding.


*** Respuesta Confuciana


Universal aesthetic sense exists through human nature and moral cultivation, requiring virtue development and cultural refinement according to Confucian aesthetic anthropology.


*** Respuesta Kantiana


Universal aesthetic sense exists through judgment structure and communicability, requiring reflective capacity and aesthetic community according to Kantian aesthetic theory.


*** Respuesta Cultural


Universal aesthetic sense does not exist with aesthetic appreciation remaining culturally relative, requiring respect for aesthetic diversity according to cultural aesthetic theory.



** What is the nature of aesthetic experience?


*** Respuesta Catolica


Aesthetic experience involves the soul's encounter with transcendental beauty (pulchrum) as a property of being itself, reflecting divine beauty through proportion, integrity, and clarity (proportio, integritas, claritas), with authentic beauty directing the soul toward divine contemplation and the source of all beauty.


*** Respuesta Protestante


Aesthetic experience reflects God's creative glory and order revealed in creation, with beauty pointing toward divine majesty and goodness, though requiring discernment to distinguish authentic beauty serving God's glory from deceptive appearances or idolatrous aesthetic experience.


*** Respuesta Ortodoxa


Aesthetic experience participates in divine beauty through energies, with liturgical aesthetics providing paradigmatic encounter with divine glory through iconographic theology, sacred music, and architectural form oriented toward theosis and mystical participation.


*** Respuesta Oriental Ortodoxa


Aesthetic experience participates in divine beauty established in the Incarnation, with liturgical aesthetics providing authentic encounter with divine glory through traditional iconography, sacred music, and architectural forms according to apostolic tradition and patristic consensus.

* Filosofia de la Religion



** Does God exist?


*** Respuesta Catolica


God's existence can be demonstrated through rational argument and natural theology, with five ways proving divine existence according to Thomistic philosophical demonstration requiring both reason and faith.


*** Respuesta Protestante


God's existence remains self-evident through creation and conscience while requiring faithful acceptance, with Scripture providing ultimate authority according to Reformed epistemological framework.


*** Respuesta Ortodoxa


God's existence transcends rational demonstration while being accessible through divine energies, requiring mystical experience and patristic wisdom according to Orthodox apophatic theology.


*** Respuesta Judia


God's existence remains fundamental to covenant relationship and ethical obligation, requiring faithful acceptance and rational investigation according to Jewish theological tradition.


*** Respuesta Islamica


God's existence (Allah) remains self-evident through creation and fitrah, requiring rational demonstration and faithful submission according to Islamic theological framework.


*** Respuesta Hindu


Divine existence (Brahman/Ishvara) remains demonstrable through philosophical argument and spiritual realization, requiring both rational investigation and contemplative practice according to Vedantic theology.


*** Respuesta Budista


Divine existence questions remain secondary to liberation from suffering, with focus on practical spirituality rather than metaphysical speculation according to Buddhist soteriological priority.


*** Respuesta Confuciana


Divine existence (Heaven/Tian) remains implicit in moral order and cosmic harmony, requiring virtue cultivation rather than theological speculation according to Confucian practical philosophy.


*** Respuesta Deist


God's existence can be demonstrated through rational argument and natural theology, requiring philosophical investigation without supernatural revelation according to deist rational religion.


*** Respuesta Atheist


God's existence lacks sufficient evidence and rational justification, requiring naturalistic explanation and scientific methodology according to atheist philosophical framework.



** What are the arguments for God's existence?


*** Respuesta Catolica


God's existence is demonstrable through natural reason via the Five Ways (motus, efficient causation, contingency, degrees of perfection, governance), with rational demonstration providing preambles to faith while supernatural revelation provides knowledge of divine mysteries beyond natural reason's capacity.


*** Respuesta Protestante


God's existence is evident through natural revelation in creation and conscience, though sinful reason requires Scripture's illumination for authentic knowledge, with rational arguments supporting but remaining subordinate to biblical revelation and divine grace.


*** Respuesta Ortodoxa


God's existence is accessible through natural reason and spiritual perception, though rational demonstration provides limited knowledge compared to mystical participation in divine energies through purified nous and liturgical experience.


*** Respuesta Judia


Arguments for God's existence include cosmological and moral arguments while emphasizing covenant relationship, requiring both rational investigation and faithful commitment according to Jewish philosophical tradition.


*** Respuesta Islamica


Arguments for God's existence include cosmological, teleological, and fitrah arguments demonstrating Allah's existence, requiring both rational demonstration and Quranic confirmation according to Islamic theology (kalam).


*** Respuesta Hindu


Arguments for God's existence include cosmological, consciousness, and scriptural arguments demonstrating Brahman/Ishvara, requiring both philosophical investigation and spiritual realization according to Vedantic theology.


*** Respuesta Budista


Arguments for God's existence remain secondary to practical liberation, with focus on Four Noble Truths rather than metaphysical speculation according to Buddhist soteriological methodology.


*** Respuesta Confuciana


Arguments for Heaven's reality include moral order and cosmic harmony, requiring virtue cultivation rather than theological demonstration according to Confucian practical philosophy.


*** Respuesta Philosophical


Arguments for God's existence include ontological, cosmological, teleological, and moral arguments requiring rational demonstration according to classical theistic philosophical tradition.


*** Respuesta Evidentialist


Arguments for God's existence require empirical evidence and scientific verification, with insufficient data supporting theistic claims according to evidentialist epistemological framework.


*** Respuesta Oriental Ortodoxa


God's existence is evident through creation and christological revelation, though rational demonstration serves supportive function while apostolic tradition and incarnational mystery provide authentic knowledge of divine reality.


*** Respuesta Is the cosmological argument sound?


Yes, the cosmological argument demonstrates God's existence as First Cause and necessary being through the principle of sufficient reason and impossibility of infinite regress in essential causation, establishing God as ipsum esse subsistens (subsistent being itself). The cosmological argument provides rational support for divine existence though remaining subordinate to biblical revelation, demonstrating creation's dependence on divine causation while Scripture provides authoritative knowledge of God's nature and will. The cosmological argument provides rational demonstration supporting sp...



** What are the arguments against God's existence?


*** Respuesta Catolica


Arguments against God's existence fail through inadequate understanding of divine nature and natural theology, requiring proper metaphysical analysis and distinction between essence and existence according to Thomistic apologetics.


*** Respuesta Protestante


Arguments against God's existence stem from sinful rebellion and intellectual pride, requiring faithful submission to Scripture and spiritual regeneration according to Reformed understanding of unbelief.


*** Respuesta Ortodoxa


Arguments against God's existence reflect rational limitations and spiritual blindness, requiring purification and mystical experience rather than purely intellectual response according to Orthodox spiritual epistemology.


*** Respuesta Judia


Arguments against God's existence challenge covenant faith while requiring rational response, with emphasis on historical experience and ethical obligation according to Jewish apologetic tradition.


*** Respuesta Islamica


Arguments against God's existence contradict fitrah and rational demonstration, requiring scholarly refutation and spiritual guidance according to Islamic apologetic methodology.


*** Respuesta Hindu


Arguments against God's existence reflect limited understanding and spiritual immaturity, requiring philosophical clarification and contemplative realization according to Vedantic apologetic approach.


*** Respuesta Budista


Arguments against God's existence remain irrelevant to liberation from suffering, with focus on practical spirituality rather than theological debate according to Buddhist methodological priority.


*** Respuesta Confuciana


Arguments against Heaven's reality contradict moral experience and cosmic order, requiring virtue cultivation and cultural wisdom according to Confucian practical approach.


*** Respuesta Atheist


Arguments against God's existence include problem of evil, lack of evidence, and naturalistic explanation, requiring rational critique and scientific methodology according to atheist philosophical framework.


*** Respuesta Agnostic


Arguments against God's existence indicate epistemological limitations and insufficient knowledge, requiring suspension of judgment according to agnostic skeptical methodology.



** What is the nature of the divine?


*** Respuesta Catolica


Divine nature consists in pure actuality (actus purus) as ipsum esse subsistens, requiring understanding of divine simplicity, infinity, and perfection according to Thomistic natural theology.


*** Respuesta Protestante


Divine nature reveals sovereign majesty and covenant faithfulness through Scripture, requiring faithful submission and theological precision according to Reformed systematic theology.


*** Respuesta Ortodoxa


Divine nature remains unknowable in essence while accessible through energies, requiring apophatic theology and mystical experience according to Orthodox patristic tradition.


*** Respuesta Judia


Divine nature transcends human comprehension while revealing covenant relationship, requiring ethical response and theological humility according to Jewish theological tradition.


*** Respuesta Islamica


Divine nature (Allah) encompasses absolute unity (tawhid) and ninety-nine beautiful names, requiring theological precision and spiritual submission according to Islamic theological framework.


*** Respuesta Hindu


Divine nature encompasses both personal (Ishvara) and impersonal (Brahman) aspects, requiring philosophical investigation and spiritual realization according to Vedantic theological understanding.


*** Respuesta Budista


Divine nature questions remain secondary to liberation methodology, with focus on Buddha-nature and enlightenment rather than metaphysical speculation according to Buddhist soteriological approach.


*** Respuesta Confuciana


Divine nature (Heaven/Tian) manifests through moral order and cosmic harmony, requiring virtue cultivation and cultural wisdom according to Confucian theological understanding.


*** Respuesta Philosophical


Divine nature requires systematic analysis of divine attributes including omniscience, omnipotence, and perfect goodness according to classical theistic philosophical framework.


*** Respuesta Process


Divine nature encompasses both eternal and temporal aspects through creative evolution, requiring dynamic understanding and relational theology according to process theological framework.


*** Respuesta What are the attributes of God?


God possesses all perfections in infinite degree - omnipotence, omniscience, perfect goodness, eternality, immutability, and simplicity - with divine attributes being really identical with divine essence while remaining conceptually distinct for human understanding. God possesses perfect attributes including omnipotence, omniscience, perfect holiness, eternality, and immutability, with divine perfections revealed in Scripture and serving divine glory while remaining ultimately incomprehensible to finite understanding. Yes, God is omnipotent as able to do whatever does not involve logical contradiction or oppose divine nature, with divine omnipotence including creation ex nihilo, miracles, and governance of all reality while respecting logical coherence and divine perfection. Yes, God is omnipotent as sovereignly able to accomplish divine will according to perfect nature, with divine power including creation, providence, and redemption while remaining consistent with divine character and biblical revelation. *** Respuesta Is God omniscient?


Yes, God is omniscient with perfect knowledge of all actual and possible reality through divine essence as pure actuality, knowing all things in divine eternity while respecting genuine contingency and human freedom within temporal succession. Yes, God is omniscient with perfect foreknowledge and sovereignty over all events according to divine decree, with divine knowledge including all actual and possible realities while maintaining human responsibility and biblical authority. Yes, God is omniscient through divine energies providing perfect knowledge, with divine omniscience accessible thr...


*** Respuesta Is God perfectly good?


Yes, God is perfectly good as pure actuality and being itself, with divine goodness being identical with divine essence and serving as source and measure of all created goodness, while divine commands express eternal law rather than arbitrary will. Yes, God is perfectly good as the standard of moral perfection revealed in Scripture, with divine goodness defining moral truth and serving as foundation for ethical obligations while expressing divine character and holy love. Yes, God is perfectly good through divine essence and energies, with divine goodness accessible through mystical particip...



** Is God personal or impersonal?


*** Respuesta Catolica


God remains supremely personal as subsistent intellect and will while transcending human personality, requiring analogical understanding and theological precision according to Thomistic divine psychology.


*** Respuesta Protestante


God reveals personal relationship and covenant faithfulness through Scripture, requiring faithful response and trinitarian understanding according to Reformed theological anthropomorphism.


*** Respuesta Ortodoxa


God remains personal in trinitarian relationships while transcending created personality, requiring mystical experience and patristic wisdom according to Orthodox trinitarian theology.


*** Respuesta Judia


God reveals personal covenant relationship while maintaining transcendent mystery, requiring ethical response and theological humility according to Jewish relational theology.


*** Respuesta Islamica


Allah remains personal through divine names and attributes while maintaining absolute transcendence, requiring proper theological understanding according to Islamic doctrinal framework.


*** Respuesta Hindu


Divine reality encompasses both personal (Saguna Brahman/Ishvara) and impersonal (Nirguna Brahman) aspects, requiring philosophical discernment according to Vedantic theological analysis.


*** Respuesta Budista


Personal/impersonal distinctions remain conceptual constructions, with focus on liberation from suffering rather than theological categorization according to Buddhist methodological approach.


*** Respuesta Confuciana


Heaven (Tian) manifests personal concern through moral order while remaining transcendent, requiring virtue cultivation and cultural wisdom according to Confucian theological understanding.


*** Respuesta Theistic


God remains essentially personal with consciousness, will, and relational capacity, requiring theistic understanding and religious relationship according to classical theistic framework.


*** Respuesta Pantheistic


Divine reality remains impersonal as cosmic substance or process, requiring naturalistic understanding and scientific methodology according to pantheistic philosophical framework.



** What are divine attributes?


*** Respuesta Catolica


Divine attributes include simplicity, infinity, immutability, eternity, omniscience, omnipotence, and perfect goodness understood analogically according to Thomistic systematic theology.


*** Respuesta Protestante


Divine attributes include sovereignty, holiness, love, justice, mercy, and faithfulness revealed through Scripture according to Reformed systematic theological framework.


*** Respuesta Ortodoxa


Divine attributes remain accessible through energies while essence remains unknowable, requiring mystical experience and patristic theology according to Orthodox apophatic tradition.


*** Respuesta Judia


Divine attributes include unity, transcendence, justice, mercy, and covenant faithfulness understood through biblical revelation according to Jewish systematic theology.


*** Respuesta Islamica


Divine attributes include ninety-nine beautiful names (asma al-husna) encompassing mercy, justice, power, and wisdom according to Islamic theological precision.


*** Respuesta Hindu


Divine attributes include sat-chit-ananda (existence-consciousness-bliss) and saguna qualities manifesting infinite perfections according to Vedantic theological analysis.


*** Respuesta Budista


Divine attribute questions remain secondary to Buddha-nature qualities including compassion, wisdom, and skillful means according to Buddhist soteriological methodology.


*** Respuesta Confuciana


Heavenly attributes include moral governance, cosmic harmony, and cultural guidance manifesting through natural order according to Confucian theological understanding.


*** Respuesta Classical Theistic


Divine attributes include perfection properties (omniscience, omnipotence, omnibenevolence) requiring systematic philosophical analysis according to classical theistic framework.


*** Respuesta Negative Theology


Divine attributes can only be described negatively through via negativa, requiring apophatic methodology and mystical theology according to negative theological tradition.



** What is the problem of evil?


*** Respuesta Catolica


Problem of evil resolves through understanding evil as privation of good and divine permission for greater good, requiring natural law analysis and providential trust according to Thomistic theodicy.


*** Respuesta Protestante


Problem of evil results from human sin and divine sovereignty, requiring faithful submission and eschatological hope according to Reformed understanding of divine providence.


*** Respuesta Ortodoxa


Problem of evil addresses through divine energies and cosmic transfiguration, requiring spiritual discernment and liturgical participation according to Orthodox theological anthropology.


*** Respuesta Judia


Problem of evil challenges covenant faith while requiring ethical response, with emphasis on historical suffering and divine justice according to Jewish theological wrestling.


*** Respuesta Islamica


Problem of evil resolves through divine wisdom and human testing, requiring submission to divine decree and moral responsibility according to Islamic theological framework.


*** Respuesta Hindu


Problem of evil explains through karmic law and spiritual evolution, requiring understanding of cosmic justice and dharmic responsibility according to Hindu theological system.


*** Respuesta Budista


Problem of evil addresses through understanding suffering's causes and liberation methodology, requiring Four Noble Truths and Eightfold Path according to Buddhist soteriological framework.


*** Respuesta Confuciana


Problem of evil challenges through moral cultivation and social responsibility, requiring virtue development and cultural transformation according to Confucian ethical approach.


*** Respuesta Free Will


Problem of evil resolves through human freedom and moral responsibility, requiring libertarian understanding and soul-making theodicy according to free will theological framework.


*** Respuesta Skeptical


Problem of evil provides evidence against divine existence or benevolence, requiring rational critique and naturalistic explanation according to skeptical philosophical methodology.



** How can evil exist if God is all-good and all-powerful?


*** Respuesta Catolica


Evil exists as privation of good permitted by God for greater good, with divine omnipotence including power to bring good from evil according to Thomistic theodicy and divine providence.


*** Respuesta Protestante


Evil exists through human sin and divine sovereignty, with God's goodness and power manifested through redemptive plan according to Reformed understanding of divine decree.


*** Respuesta Ortodoxa


Evil exists through misuse of freedom while God's goodness works cosmic transfiguration, requiring mystical understanding and eschatological hope according to Orthodox theological framework.


*** Respuesta Judia


Evil exists as challenge to covenant faith while divine justice remains ultimate, requiring faithful wrestling and ethical response according to Jewish theological tradition.


*** Respuesta Islamica


Evil exists as divine test and human responsibility while Allah's wisdom encompasses all, requiring submission and moral accountability according to Islamic theological understanding.


*** Respuesta Hindu


Evil exists through karmic consequences and spiritual ignorance while divine goodness guides cosmic evolution, requiring dharmic understanding and spiritual practice according to Hindu theodicy.


*** Respuesta Budista


Evil exists through ignorance and craving while liberation remains possible, requiring understanding of suffering's causes and path to freedom according to Buddhist analysis.


*** Respuesta Confuciana


Evil exists through moral failure and social disorder while Heaven's goodness guides moral transformation, requiring virtue cultivation according to Confucian ethical framework.


*** Respuesta Process


Evil exists through creative risk and temporal limitation while divine goodness works persuasive love, requiring dynamic understanding according to process theological framework.


*** Respuesta Logical


Evil's existence logically contradicts divine omnipotence and perfect goodness, requiring abandonment of classical theism according to logical problem of evil argument.



** Does suffering have meaning?


*** Respuesta Catolica


Suffering achieves meaning through participation in Christ's passion and redemptive value, requiring spiritual transformation and offering for others according to Catholic understanding of redemptive suffering.


*** Respuesta Protestante


Suffering achieves meaning through divine sovereignty and sanctification, requiring faithful endurance and spiritual growth according to Reformed theology of affliction.


*** Respuesta Ortodoxa


Suffering achieves meaning through theotic transformation and cosmic healing, requiring ascetical discipline and mystical participation according to Orthodox spiritual theology.


*** Respuesta Judia


Suffering challenges meaning while requiring ethical response and covenant faithfulness, with emphasis on historical memory and divine justice according to Jewish theological reflection.


*** Respuesta Islamica


Suffering achieves meaning through divine testing and spiritual purification, requiring patience (sabr) and submission according to Islamic understanding of tribulation.


*** Respuesta Hindu


Suffering achieves meaning through karmic purification and spiritual evolution, requiring dharmic acceptance and contemplative practice according to Hindu understanding of dukkha.


*** Respuesta Budista


Suffering achieves meaning through understanding its causes and liberation methodology, requiring mindfulness and compassionate response according to Buddhist Four Noble Truths.


*** Respuesta Confuciana


Suffering achieves meaning through moral cultivation and social responsibility, requiring virtue development and cultural transformation according to Confucian ethical framework.


*** Respuesta Existencialista


Suffering achieves meaning through authentic choice and personal responsibility, requiring courageous affirmation and creative response according to existentialist philosophical framework.


*** Respuesta Nihilistic


Suffering lacks inherent meaning in absurd universe, requiring honest acknowledgment of meaninglessness according to nihilistic philosophical perspective.



* Conclusion
:PROPERTIES:
:UNNUMBERED: t
:END:

** Patrones que emergen

A traves de todas las tradiciones, ciertos temas aparecen una y otra vez:

1. *La busqueda de lo trascendente* - Ya sea Dios, Brahman, el Tao, o la Razon universal, las tradiciones reconocen algo que supera la experiencia ordinaria.

2. *La importancia de la virtud* - Todas las tradiciones valoran el cultivo del caracter moral, aunque difieran sobre que virtudes son centrales.

3. *La conexion entre conocimiento y transformacion* - El verdadero conocimiento no es meramente intelectual sino transformador de la persona.

4. *La tension entre individuo y comunidad* - Las tradiciones luchan por equilibrar la autonomia personal con la responsabilidad social.

** Diferencias irreducibles

Sin embargo, las diferencias son reales y significativas:

- *Sobre lo divino*: Personal vs. impersonal, uno vs. muchos, trascendente vs. inmanente
- *Sobre el conocimiento*: Revelacion vs. razon vs. experiencia mistica
- *Sobre la etica*: Mandato divino vs. ley natural vs. consecuencias
- *Sobre el destino humano*: Salvacion vs. liberacion vs. disolucion

** Una ultima reflexion

Estas preguntas no tienen respuestas definitivas porque tocan los limites de la comprension humana. Cada tradicion representa el esfuerzo sincero de seres humanos por dar sentido a la existencia.

La humildad intelectual es quiza la mayor leccion: reconocer que ninguna tradicion posee toda la verdad, y que el dialogo respetuoso entre perspectivas diferentes enriquece nuestra comprension comun.

* Glosario
:PROPERTIES:
:UNNUMBERED: t
:END:

- *Brahman* - En el hinduismo, la realidad ultima, absoluta e infinita
- *Dharma* - Ley cosmica, deber moral, ensenanza espiritual (hinduismo/budismo)
- *Nirvana* - Estado de liberacion del sufrimiento y el ciclo de renacimientos (budismo)
- *Tao* - El camino, principio cosmico inefable que subyace a toda realidad (taoismo)
- *Theosis* - Divinizacion o deificacion del ser humano (cristianismo oriental)
- *Tawhid* - La unicidad absoluta de Dios (islam)
- *Torah* - La ley revelada, los cinco libros de Moises (judaismo)
- *Logos* - Razon universal, palabra divina (filosofia griega/cristianismo)
- *Karma* - Ley de causa y efecto moral (hinduismo/budismo)
- *Samsara* - Ciclo de nacimiento, muerte y renacimiento (hinduismo/budismo)
